<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Passchendaele&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Passchendaele</i> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ən/: 'on' in 'button'">ən</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span>/</a></span></span> is the common English title. The British <i>Battle Nomenclature Committee</i> called the Flanders offensives of 1917, The Battle of Messines 1917 <span class="nowrap">(7–14 June)</span> and The Battles of Ypres 1917 <span class="nowrap">(31 July – 10 November).</span><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEdmonds1991iii_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdmonds1991iii-1">[1]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The series of battles are known to the British as The Battle of Messines 1917 <span class="nowrap">(7–14 June),</span> The Battle of Pilckem Ridge <span class="nowrap">(31 July – 2 August),</span> the Battle of Langemarck <span class="nowrap">(16–18 August),</span> The Battle of Menin Road Ridge <span class="nowrap">(20–25 September),</span> the Battle of Polygon Wood <span class="nowrap">(26 September – 3 October)</span> the Battle of Broodseinde (4 October), the Battle of Poelcappelle (9 October), the First Battle of Passchendaele (12 October) and the Second Battle of Passchendaele <span class="nowrap">(26 October – 10 November)</span> and referred to in German works as (<span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Kampf um den Wijtschatebogen</i></span>) (The Battle of the Wijtschate Salient) and the (<span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Flandernschlacht</i></span>) (Battle of Flanders) in five periods, First Battle of Flanders <span class="nowrap">(31 July – 9 August),</span> Second Battle of Flanders <span class="nowrap">(9–25 August),</span> Third Battle of Flanders <span class="nowrap">(20 September – 8 October)</span> Fourth Battle of Flanders <span class="nowrap">(9–21 October)</span> and Fifth Battle of Flanders <span class="nowrap">(22 October – 5 December).</span><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEdmonds1991iii_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdmonds1991iii-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheldon2007xiv_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheldon2007xiv-3">[2]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-42">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">After mutinies had begun in the French armies, the British cabinet felt compelled to endorse the Flanders offensive, in the hope that more refusals to fight could be "averted by a great [military] success". Haig wrote that if the Allies could win the war in 1917, "the chief people to suffer would be the socialists".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMillman200161_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMillman200161-40">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrench1995119.E2.80.93122.2C_92.E2.80.9393.2C_146_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrench1995119.E2.80.93122.2C_92.E2.80.9393.2C_146-41">[39]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-95"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-95">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/4th_Guards_Infantry_Division_(German_Empire)" title="4th Guards Infantry Division (German Empire)">4th Guards Division</a>, <a href="/wiki/4th_Royal_Bavarian_Division" title="4th Royal Bavarian Division">4th Bavarian Division</a>, <a href="/wiki/6th_Royal_Bavarian_Division" title="6th Royal Bavarian Division">6th Bavarian Division</a>, <a href="/wiki/10th_Ersatz_Division_(German_Empire)" title="10th Ersatz Division (German Empire)">10th Ersatz Division</a>, <a href="/wiki/16th_Division_(German_Empire)" title="16th Division (German Empire)">16th Division</a>, <a href="/wiki/19th_Reserve_Division_(German_Empire)" title="19th Reserve Division (German Empire)">19th Reserve Division</a>, <a href="/wiki/20th_Division_(German_Empire)" title="20th Division (German Empire)">20th Division</a>, 187th Division, 195th Division and <a href="/wiki/45th_Reserve_Division_(German_Empire)" title="45th Reserve Division (German Empire)">45th Reserve Division</a> took part in the battle.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUSWD1920_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUSWD1920-94">[91]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-124"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-124">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">195th, 16th, 4th Bavarian, 18th, 227th, 240th, 187th and 22nd Reserve divisions).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUSWD1920_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUSWD1920-94">[91]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-147"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-147">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">German troops engaged were from the 239th, 39th, 4th, 44th Reserve, 7th, 11th, 11th Bavarian, 238th, 199th, 27th, 185th, 111th and 40th divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUSWD1920_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUSWD1920-94">[91]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-151"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-151">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">German casualties were counted in ten-day periods. A discrepancy of <span class="nowrap">27,000 fewer</span> casualties recorded in the <i>Sanitätsbericht</i> could not be explained by the Reichsarchiv historians.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReichsarchiv194296_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReichsarchiv194296-150">[144]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>
